<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">North East of England Process Industry Cluster</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Advert" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>contains content that is written like <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_a_soapbox_or_means_of_promotion" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">an advertisement</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit">improve it</a> by removing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Spam" title="Wikipedia:Spam">promotional content</a> and inappropriate <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links" title="Wikipedia:External links">external links</a>, and by adding encyclopedic content written from a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">neutral point of view</a>.</span> <small><i>(June 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>

<p>The <b>North East of England Process Industry Cluster</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup>   (<b>NEPIC</b>) is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_clusters" title="Economic clusters">economic cluster</a> created following the industrial cluster ideas and strategy of <a href="/wiki/Michael_Porter" title="Michael Porter">Michael Porter</a>. This Process Industry <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_clusters" title="Economic clusters">Cluster</a> has been created by the chemistry using industries based in <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East England</a> where more than 1,400 companies are based in the <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain" title="Supply chain">supply chain</a> of the sector. The sector has over 35,000 direct employees and some 190,000 indirect employees in the northeast of England and together they represent over one third of the industrial economy of the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Companies in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_clusters" title="Economic clusters">Cluster</a> manufacture 50% of the UK's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrochemicals" title="Petrochemicals">Petrochemicals</a> and 35% of the UK's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals" title="Pharmaceuticals">Pharmaceuticals</a> and they significantly contribute towards making the region the only net <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exporting" title="Exporting">exporting</a> region of the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The region has over £13 billion of exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>NEPIC was created in 2004 by the leaders of local chemistry based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Process_industry" title="Process industry">process industry</a> companies that are based in the northeast of England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The aim of the organisation being to represent and coordinate industry's collaborative activities on the wide ranging issues that impact on the future and performance of the energy intensive process sector, which includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrochemicals" title="Petrochemicals">petrochemicals</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specialty_chemicals" title="Specialty chemicals">specialty chemicals</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polymers" title="Polymers">polymers</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals" title="Pharmaceuticals">pharmaceuticals</a>; <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewables" title="Renewables">renewables</a>. These issues include renewable and more <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable energy</a> opportunities,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">innovation</a> and R&amp;D interests,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> energy pricing capacity and availability,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> carbon taxation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> and carbon emission reduction technologies <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> such as <a href="/wiki/Carbon_capture_and_storage" title="Carbon capture and storage">carbon capture and storage</a> (CCS),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> graduate and technician skills for the sector <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> and industry growth to ensure that the region remains a globally important location for the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemical industry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>NEPIC has been recognised by the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Industries_Association" title="Chemical Industries Association">Chemical Industries Association</a> (CIA) in the UK for its work in informing stakeholders about the sector<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and by the professional institutions in the UK for its engagement and representation of industry issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The Northeast of England is recognised and promoted by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Trade" title="Department for International Trade">Department for International Trade</a> (DIT)( formerly UK Trade and Investment (UKTI)) arm of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_Government" title="UK Government">UK Government</a> as a leading location in the UK for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_Direct_Investment" title="Foreign Direct Investment">Foreign Direct Investment</a>(FDI) into the chemistry using industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since its formation NEPIC has participated in European <a href="/wiki/Cluster_development" title="Cluster development">Cluster development</a> programmes. During 2012 NEPIC was initially audited by the European Secretariat for Cluster Analysis (ESCA) and in March 2014 achieved the Gold Label standard for Cluster management under this quality management scheme. NEPIC is classified by ESCA as a <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">innovation</a> cluster and was the first UK cluster to achieve this Gold Label status and the 37th Cluster to do so in Europe. By March 2014 there were 490 EU Cluster organisations accredited by ESCA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> By September 2014 the European Secretariat for Cluster Analysis reported that more than 600 Clusters had been audited and in their report, entitled "Cluster Organisations in Europe - insights from Bronze and Gold Label Assessments", cited the NEPIC Members Directory as best practice as a Cluster global marketing tool.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> On 20 October 2014 at the European Commission's Bi-annual European Cluster Conference, policy makers, analysts and Cluster managers, from all business and industry sectors across Europe, named Dr Stan Higgins, NEPIC CEO, as European Cluster Manager of the Year 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> NEPIC was reassessed by ESCA during 2016 and is validated as a Gold Label Cluster until February 2019 when the Cluster's management organisation has to undergo its next quality assessment. By March 2017 986 Clusters had been awarded Bronze, Silver and Gold Labels from 40 countries. 81 of which are Gold Label.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>NEPIC is led by industry through its Industry Leadership Team. These industry leaders at intervals of their choosing elect a person to be the Chair of NEPIC. Since its inception the cluster has been Chaired by Ian Shott CBE, Robert Coxon OBE,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Paul Booth MBE<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and most recently former MP <a href="/wiki/Ian_Swales" title="Ian Swales">Ian Swales</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> who is the current chair person. Dr Stan Higgins has been NEPIC's Chief Executive Officer (CEO) since its formation in 2004. Dr Higgins announced that he is to retire during 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> On 1 June 2017 NEPIC announced that former Chair of the UK Parliamentary Business Committee and labour MP <a href="/wiki/Iain_Wright" title="Iain Wright">Iain Wright</a> is to become the CEO of NEPIC<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Supporting_and_developing_an_extensive_supply_chain"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Supporting and developing an extensive supply chain</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Role_of_clusters_such_as_NEPIC_in_globalised_industries"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Role of clusters such as NEPIC in globalised industries</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stakeholder_activity">Stakeholder activity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Stakeholder activity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>NEPIC's work with stakeholders of the process industry in its region includes encouraging school children to study Science, Engineering, Technology and Mathematics (STEM subjects). It has run programmes for both secondary and primary school children. In showing the relevance of science and industry to primary school children NEPIC promotes the Children Challenging Industry programme operated by the Chemical Industry Education Unit at York University. The Cluster, in March 2009, enabled a group of school children from Morpeth, Northumberland,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> to record in the Guinness Book of Records the world's largest mathematics class. The Cluster also supports a Fellowship to encourage young scientists and engineers to experience Parliamentary processes by spending time in the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Office_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Parliamentary Office of Science and Technology">Parliamentary Office of Science and Technology</a> (POST), based in the Houses of Parliament, Westminster, London. This annual Fellowship<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> commemorates the life of Chemical Engineer and Member of Parliament, <a href="/wiki/Ashok_Kumar_(British_politician)" title="Ashok Kumar (British politician)">Ashok Kumar</a>, who as MP for Middlesbrough South and East Cleveland, was a supporter of both the Cluster and also of the co-sponsors of the Fellowship, the <a href="/wiki/Institution_of_Chemical_Engineers" title="Institution of Chemical Engineers">Institution of Chemical Engineers</a>. In 2017 the 6th Ashok Kumar Fellow had been appointed to work with at POST she was a postgraduate engineering student, Erin Johnson, from Imperial College, London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_Awards">Annual Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Annual Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>NEPIC hold a well attended Annual Awards Dinner that further cements its links to stakeholders. Awards of £1000 are given to 5 Young Achievers from within its key sectors of Petrochemicals, Fine &amp; Specialty Chemicals, Pharmaceuticals, Biotechnology and Supply Chain. Similarly 3 x £1000 prizes are given to 3 top Apprentices from the Cluster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The Cluster gives awards to the value of £2000 to companies for outstanding industrial performance in Innovation, Manufacturing Sustainability and Environmental Activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> However, the award winning organisations must nominate a school to receive their prize money and use the funding for a science related project in that school. Each year a £2000 Award is given directly to a local school for an Environmental project that its pupils have developed and shown that it can be implemented with the prize. 
The Cluster has established a prestigious Outstanding Contribution Award for an individual who in their career has made a significant contribution to the Industry in Northeast England. In 2009 this was won by Thomas Swan of Thomas Swan Ltd for his establishment of Children Challenging Industry; 2010 Garren Denham of BKE Mowlem for improving contractor safety performance; 2011 George Ritchie of Sembcorp for championing skills particularly through apprenticeships; 2012 Dr Robert Hardy for establishing and growing Aesica Pharmaceuticals in the region; 2013 Subhash Chaudharry of Fujifilm Dyosynth Biologics for his contribution to biotech engineering; 2014 Ken Home for his development of KHome an international engineering company in the region. 2015 Mark Lewis, Technical Manager of NEPIC, who during his career had helped ICI divest its engineering interests, set up the Process Industry Centre for Manufacturing Excellence (PICME)and led NEPICs technical support for the sector. Martin Inskip Plant Director of Merck Sharp &amp; Dhome (MSD) joined the roll of honour of the sector's greatest contributors as he collected the 2016 award for Outstanding Contribution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> David Hodgson Health Safety &amp; Environment Manager of Sterling Pharma Solutions of Dudley, Cramlington, Northumberland won the 2017 Outstanding Contribution Award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> All these outstanding contributors also donated their £2000 prizes to local school projects.   
</p><p>Over the 8 years to 2014 the NEPIC Annual Dinner has awarded £158k in prize money that includes £62k to the sectors rising young stars, £90k to support STEM projects within 45 local schools and £6,000 in support of new Exporters in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> In 2017 the cumulative prize money given out to award winners at the NEPIC awards reached £200,000. £66,000 to young achievers and apprentices and £134,000 to company award winners all of the money going to the companies being donated to School projects for Science, Technology, Engineering and Mathematics (STEM) Projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> This means that 67 X £2000 school projects had been supported by 2017.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cluster_Strategy_for_Growth">Cluster Strategy for Growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cluster Strategy for Growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Industry Leadership Council of NEPIC regularly revisits the Cluster's Strategy for Growth, after first publishing it in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> NEPIC and the Industrialists concerned were commended for this work in the UK Parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The NEPIC Strategy is published and approved at the organisation's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annual_General_Meeting" title="Annual General Meeting">Annual General Meeting</a> (AGM). The most recent strategy was published in December 2012.
</p><p>The Cluster's ongoing strategic themes include:
</p>
<ul><li>1. Continue Growth Activities - attract &amp; develop investment.</li>
<li>2. Support the National Skills Academy for the Process Industry skills development activities and - grow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apprenticeships" title="Apprenticeships">apprenticeships</a>.</li>
<li>3. Grow Membership - develop supply chain interaction &amp; sales.</li>
<li>4. Continue to provide a 'Voice for the Sector'.</li></ul>
<p>The new strategic themes introduced in 2012 were:
</p>
<ul><li>1. Increase International awareness of the industry in the region.</li>
<li>2. Improve connectivity and help bring alignment with other UK industry bodies.</li>
<li>3. Develop or Support innovative projects for the rejuvenation, sustainability and growth of the industries in the process sector.</li>
<li>4. Grow participation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Small_%26_medium_enterprises" title="Small &amp; medium enterprises">Small &amp; Medium Enterprises</a>(SMEs) in all the strategic themes of the Sector.</li></ul>
<p>The Cluster's executive team are challenged to create and deliver projects and activities that deliver on these themes.
</p>
<h2><span id="Measuring_NEPIC.27s_performance"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Measuring_NEPIC's_performance">Measuring NEPIC's performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Measuring NEPIC's performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GVA_creation">GVA creation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: GVA creation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>NEPIC's overall performance against its strategy and as a Cluster body is measured in terms of economic development within its region. This is monitored by its Industry Leadership Council and public sector observers through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Key_performance_indicators" title="Key performance indicators">key performance indicators</a> (KPIs). These mostly relate to the cluster's results in attracting and assisting both indigenous and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> (FDI) investment, as well as business growth in the local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Small_%26_medium_enterprises" title="Small &amp; medium enterprises">SME</a> supply chain and any resulting job creation. These factors contribute to an overall performance measure of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_Value_Added" title="Gross Value Added">Gross Value Added</a> (GVA). Results from the six year period 2005 to 2011 show that through its industry led activities, by 2017, NEPIC's activities are contributing significant levels of GVA to its local economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_economy" title="UK economy">UK economy</a>. In December 2013 NEPIC reported to its local Members of Parliament that since 2005 the Cluster had secured 83 significant investments and 4,000 jobs which now contributes more than £2 billion GVA to the local and UK economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The ongoing work of the Cluster particularly with the Small &amp; Medium Size (SME) business community via the Clusters Business Acceleration for SMEs (BASME) project has seen the Clusters impact on its local economy grow to £2.5 Billion of GVA per annum by 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> By 2017 the total GVA contribution of NEPIC had climbed to £3.34 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Process_industry_investment">Process industry investment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Process industry investment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Between 2005 and 2013 the NEPIC, cluster members, and its local authority partners helped to secure 83 significant investments into the process industry in the region totalling £3.7 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The companies making significant investment during this period into the Cluster footprint include:
</p>
