<p>Many of the above projects and those of other NEPIC member companies have been assisted in their investment plans by grants made available by the United Kingdom Government. The Regional Growth Fund (RGF) has supported many projects within the Cluster footprint.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>By 2017 the Cluster reported that it has been involved in landing 95 process industry investments into its region worth well over £4 Billion and adding 5000 jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Collaborative_projects">Collaborative projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Collaborative projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>NEPIC has participated in a number of <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> funded cluster collaboration projects and collaborative innovation projects, thereby enabling its members to participate and access the benchmarking and business best practice that is being developed and shared. On some occasions NEPIC participates in the role as project leader/manager and in others as a partner organisation. An example of a Cluster collaboration in which NEPIC is a partner is the WIINTECH project, a worldwide intercluster initiative for new materials and processes focused on clean technologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> This collaborative project is aimed at building a common international strategy between 8 leading European clusters and to foster inter-cluster and transnational partnerships, extending international cooperation and developing a joint inter-cluster projects in areas such as technology and industrial partnerships, training &amp; skills development, technology transfer, workforce and business mobility and business mentoring. NEPIC and the other Clusters involved have undertaken joint market visits to Japan, USA, Korea, Brazil, and India to promote the EU process industries while focusing on fast growing lead markets such as clean technology. The LOCIMAP collaboration on the other hand is a project that is being led and managed by NEPIC with 13 international partners who together are investigating best practice and developing new ideas for the development of more efficient industrial parks in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Innovation_strategy">Innovation strategy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Innovation strategy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Research has shown that companies are eight times more innovative when working in a collaborative "cluster" environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> As part of the NEPIC Cluster Strategy for Growth, the Northeast Regional Innovation Strategy for the Chemistry-Using Process Industries was created. The innovation study and strategy was first published in 2005<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> and reviewed in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> It was created by the NEPIC Innovation Team of industrialists and academics.
</p><p>This work outlined a set of actions for stakeholders which have fundamentally changed the innovation performance of the region.  These were:
</p>
<ol><li>Provide market and industry input into the direction of research and hence the need for a practical forum to discuss market trends and future industry needs</li>
<li>Support and develop indigenous business and technical innovation and help turn these into economic growth</li>
<li>Enable access to critical facilities and equipment. Recognising that access can sometimes be cost prohibitive</li>
<li>Do more to attract corporate R&amp;D centres to the region in order to move the region towards the achievement of 'critical mass' in different technologies</li>
<li>Help our Universities attract world class academics to the region. Recognising that having world class capability at a local university can, over time, have significant influence on the competence of local industry</li>
<li>Work to strengthen supply chains and customer networks in the region</li></ol>
<p>The NEPIC innovation strategy led to studies into the establishment of biorefinery activity within the North East of England Process Industry Cluster (NEPIC) which is being taken forward by the Cluster's Bioresources Team. It also identified the potential of the region to create innovation centres to support the process sector into the future.
</p><p>The NEPIC Innovation Strategy established the region's industrial and academic innovation strengths within the <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> based process sector. The work informed both public and private interests and has led directly to the creation of several innovation centres that are now managed through a national "<a href="/wiki/Catapult_centres" title="Catapult centres">catapult</a>" organisation – the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Process_Innovation" title="Centre for Process Innovation">Centre for Process Innovation</a> – based at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilton_Centre" title="Wilton Centre">Wilton Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Redcar" title="Redcar">Redcar</a> on <a href="/wiki/Teesside" title="Teesside">Teesside</a>. These are the National Industrial Biotechnology Facility,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> the National Biologics Manufacturing Centre,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Printable_Electronics_Technology_Centre" title="Printable Electronics Technology Centre">Printable Electronics Technology Centre</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> the Anaerobic Digestion Development Centre<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> the Sustainable Technology Centre,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> and the Thermal Technologies Centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> All of these leading technology centres are facilities based on Teesside. They have "<a href="/wiki/Plug_and_play" title="Plug and play">plug and play</a>" scale up facilities in most <a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">chemical engineering</a> and biotech engineering <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unit_operations" title="Unit operations">unit operations</a>. They have been built as open access innovation facilities utilising over £200 million of UK Government funding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> All of these facilities are based in the North East of England Process Industry Cluster footprint in the north-east of England.
</p><p>NEPIC signposts industry towards academic programmes, projects and capability, particularity within the universities in northeast England. Arising from this Cluster activity, in September 2015, NEPIC created an innovative event enabling 90 academics to present their interests and capabilities to industry in one day; thus providing a time-efficient way to form connections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_support">Business support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Business support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>NEPIC provides technical, funding and business advice to new investors and indigenous businesses.
</p><p>To assist with industry attraction and growth, NEPIC supports companies in securing their major capital projects, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Management_buyouts" title="Management buyouts">management buyouts (MBO)</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Start-up_company" title="Start-up company">start-ups</a>. The Cluster provides intelligence on local supply chain capabilities in areas such as site location, planning, infrastructure, raw material sourcing, engineering, logistics, measurement science, workforce development and legal advice. To deliver projects NEPIC partners with its <a href="/wiki/Local_enterprise_partnership" title="Local enterprise partnership">Local Enterprise Partnerships</a> (LEP) Tees Valley Unlimited and the North East LEP (NELEP). It works internationally to attract investment and partners with other European locations for the chemical industry through the <a href="/wiki/European_Chemical_Site_Promotion_Platform" title="European Chemical Site Promotion Platform">European Chemical Site Promotion Platform</a>(ECSPP).
</p><p>In line with the Cluster's strategy, NEPIC manages several business support products to help <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Small_%26_medium_enterprises" title="Small &amp; medium enterprises">SMEs</a> grow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The Cluster  secured a Regional Growth Fund project to mentor 400 SMEs in this region into new business within the process sector. This is the Business Acceleration for SMEs (BASME) project through which 1000 jobs were created in the process sector supply chain over 3 years. More than 200 SME's signed up to this programme in the first 18 months and created over 170 jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The BASME programme has enabled NEPIC to increase the interaction between process industry companies and their local supply chain such that after 30 months 327 SMEs had engaged with it adding 425 jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> When complete, over 3 years, the BASME project reported that it had worked with 423 SMEs and helped them with business development that resulted in 1011 jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>Similarly NEPIC created a programme to mentor 120 SMEs to improve their carbon efficiency and to accredit their sustainability credentials. This  enabled some of NEPIC's SME member's supply chain data to be available to Tier 1 companies which from 2013 onwards, in the UK, are expected to have a mandatory requirement to supply their <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprints</a> on an annual basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> NEPIC's scheme called Developing Low Carbon Sustainable Industry (DEELOCSI) receives financial support from the <a href="/wiki/European_Regional_Development_Fund" title="European Regional Development Fund">European Regional Development Fund</a> (ERDF) of the European Union.
</p><p>To further encourage SMEs in the northeast of England to Export, NEPIC collaborated with the North East Chamber of Commerce (NECC) and RTC North Limited to create a jointly owned subsidiary company Go Global Limited to manage the contract they had to deliver the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UKTI" title="UKTI">United Kingdom Trade &amp; Investment</a> (UKTI) (2016 onwards UKTI became the Department for International Trade - DIT), Government funded, support products and programme for all business sectors in their region. The UKTI business support products, to help grow international trade, are aimed at supporting individual SMEs to grow their exports and they also support the Cluster and its members with <a href="/wiki/Trade_mission" title="Trade mission">trade missions</a> to new markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>In order to share knowledge with and support other business sectors in the northeast of England, NEPIC is a member of the Northern Business Forum (NBF). This business led forum also links the Cluster to wider business issues, both locally and nationally, through the local &amp; national business membership organisations represented. Members of the forum include the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Small_Businesses" title="Federation of Small Businesses">Federation of Small Businesses</a> (FSB), <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_British_Industry" title="Confederation of British Industry">Confederation of British Industry</a> (CBI) North East, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Engineering_Employers_Federation" title="Engineering Employers Federation">Engineering Employers Federation</a> Northern (EEF), The <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Directors" title="Institute of Directors">Institute of Directors</a> (IOD), The North East Chamber of Commerce (NECC), Service Network, RTC North and NEPIC. The <a href="/wiki/Association_of_North_East_Councils" title="Association of North East Councils">Association of North East Councils</a> (ANEC) are amongst the observers of the forum.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Large-scale_integrated_chemical_processing_on_Teesside">Large-scale integrated chemical processing on Teesside</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Large-scale integrated chemical processing on Teesside">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The larger, and in a number of instances, integrated chemical producers in the NEPIC Cluster are based on <a href="/wiki/Teesside" title="Teesside">Teesside</a> on three large chemical sites around the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/River_Tees" title="River Tees">River Tees</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wilton,_Redcar_and_Cleveland" title="Wilton, Redcar and Cleveland">Wilton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billingham" title="Billingham">Billingham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seal_Sands" title="Seal Sands">Seal Sands</a> that were formerly owned and operated by Imperial Chemical Industries (ICI). These locations have a long history of large scale chemical manufacturing even before the creation of ICI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The large scale manufacturing companies operating on these sites are sometimes called "<a href="/wiki/Commodity_chemicals" title="Commodity chemicals">commodity chemical manufacturers</a>" and they make products such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrochemicals" title="Petrochemicals">petrochemicals</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertilizers" title="Fertilizers">fertilizers</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polymers" title="Polymers">polymers</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_River_Tees_and_Teesport">The River Tees and Teesport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The River Tees and Teesport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Teesport" title="Teesport">Teesport</a> is based on the <a href="/wiki/River_Tees" title="River Tees">River Tees</a> and is currently the third largest port in the United Kingdom, and amongst the ten biggest in Western Europe. This port handles over 56 million tonnes of goods per annum which are mainly associated with the local petrochemical, chemical and steel processing industries. The port is an important piece of logistical infrastructure for the NEPIC cluster of process companies.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Integrated_Manufacturers_Group">Integrated Manufacturers Group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Integrated Manufacturers Group">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The large scale, commodity chemical producers on <a href="/wiki/Teesside" title="Teesside">Teesside</a> work through NEPIC's Integrated Manufacturers Group (IMG) where they exchange information on infrastructure issues and also share intelligence on engineering resources for large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maintenance,_repair,_and_operations" title="Maintenance, repair, and operations">maintenance / overhauls</a> and capital investment projects. Such projects in the chemical process sector can require hundreds of additional contract engineers for short intense periods of time and this requires extensive engineering planning. The maintenance of <a href="/wiki/Chemical_plant" title="Chemical plant">chemical plant</a>  is an engineering profession in its own right.
</p>
<h2><span id="Carbon_Capture_and_Storage_.28CCS.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Carbon_Capture_and_Storage_(CCS)">Carbon Capture and Storage (CCS)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Carbon Capture and Storage (CCS)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The NEPIC IMG of manufacturers are amongst the largest single point producers of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> in the United Kingdom and they have created within NEPIC the Process Industry Carbon Capture and Storage Initiative (PICCSI) to study the possibility of a <a href="/wiki/Carbon_capture_and_storage" title="Carbon capture and storage">carbon capture and storage</a> (CCS) solution being provided for industry on Teesside as well as for any carbon based energy production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> This CCS technology option is being considered as a result of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> regulations and the <a href="/wiki/Carbon_tax" title="Carbon tax">carbon taxation</a> that could become a prohibitive cost for such energy intensive industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p>NEPIC's persistent message, through its PICCSI group, that CCS is an important technology for the sustainability of energy intensive and carbon intensive industries in the UK such as chemical, polymer and fertilizer manufacturing, was endorsed during December 2013 by the UK Government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Until then CCS was only seen as a way of limiting carbon dioxide emissions from power generation, but with the Government's approval of the Tees Valley City Deal it included money for the industry to develop its early engineering study to determine CCS implementation costs and operating parameters. The process industry in the Tees Valley sees opportunities not only to store the carbon but also the potential to use the gas for other industrial uses, such as advanced oil recovery, manufacturing polycarbonates for plastics and battery electrolytes etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>The work of the Cluster on Industrial Carbon Capture and Storage (ICCS) has received support from the UK Government through the Local Enterprise Partnership Tees Valley Unlimited. 6 Industrial Members of the NEPIC Cluster BOC-Linde, CF Fertilizers (formerly GrowHow), Lotte Chemicals, Sembcorp Utilities and SABIC <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> are part of a project called "The Teesside Collective". A project was undertaken on behalf of the sector to determine the potential for a ICCS system. The study outlined the engineering cost of a system, the business case and investment mechanisms that would need to be addressed in establishing an operating ICCS system. This report was delivered to the UK Government on 1 July 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Teesside Collective project identifies that 5.6% of the UK's industrial emissions of Carbon Dioxide (CO2)comes from the Teesside Region and that this location has 5 of the UK's top 25 CO2 emitting plants, concluding that Teesside is the most concentrated industrial cluster in the UK making an ICCS network technically feasible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The report states that by using existing and proven technologies, an initial 2.8m t/y of CO2 could be captured, a quarter of Teesside's total CO2 emissions, and store it permanently in aquifers beneath the North Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> CO2 gas is already collected on Teesside for commercial use by some of NEPIC's members and in capturing the gas for sequestration via ICCS implementation needs only to scale up of existing technologies not new ones. A future ICCS network would encourage investment from companies whose processes cannot avoid CO2 emissions, as well as from new industries that may utilise CO2 as a raw material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Early stage design contracts have been awarded to understand engineering and running costs of an ICCS system on Teesside.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> These studies show that a viable finance proposal is possible to support a CCS network based on Teesside. The study suggests that the cost of a Teesside-based ICCS system including access to a transportation and storage network would be £58 per tonne of CO2 and compares this to Government subsidy given to  offshore wind at £200/tCO2 and £128/tCO2 for nuclear power. This work proclaims that the Tees Valley could be "the birthplace of vital clean industrial growth, attracting inward investment and job creation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shale_gas_and_underground_coal_gasification">Shale gas and underground coal gasification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Shale gas and underground coal gasification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>NEPIC members are also studying the prospect of energy production from <a href="/wiki/Unconventional_gas" title="Unconventional gas">unconventional gas</a> sources including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_from_waste" title="Energy from waste">energy from waste</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">energy from biomass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shale_gas" title="Shale gas">shale gas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coal_gasification" title="Coal gasification">underground coal gasification</a>. Several energy from waste plants are already present in this region and more are being constructed. The region is close to large reserves of <a href="/wiki/Shale_gas" title="Shale gas">shale gas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> and commercial exploitation of these reserves is being considered. The shale gas deposits close to this region that are available for exploitation by the process known as "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fracking" title="Fracking">fracking</a>" exceed 1.3 quadrillion cubic feet of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> although not all of this will be extractable. The extraction of shale gas in the UK has been the subject of two major reports, one from the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Directors" title="Institute of Directors">Institute of Directors</a> called "Getting Shale Gas Working" and one from the UK Government entitled the "Bowland Shale Gas Study".  In addition, the region has substantial unexploited coal reserves in the <a href="/wiki/Durham_Coalfield" title="Durham Coalfield">Durham Coalfield</a> and companies are developing plans to exploit this using modern clean technologies for underground coal gasification (UCG).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Linking technologies for UGC or other gas extraction from local coalfields to carbon dioxide capture technologies like those described in the "Teesside Collective Project"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> gives rise to the prospect of "Clean Coal" as a source of raw materials for the chemical sector in the northeast of England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Skills_.26_education"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Skills_&amp;_education">Skills &amp; education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Skills &amp; education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quality_skills">Quality skills</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Quality skills">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>NEPIC has taken a lead in skills development and are encouraging young people into science and engineering.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The Cluster's Skills Industry Leadership Team developed a Skills Strategy to support the growth of the sector and this led directly to the creation of the National Skills Academy for the Process Industries (NSAPI) which has its head office in Darlington in the region and is part of the COGENT Sector Skills Council (COGENT SSC). COGENT and NSAPI developed skills profiles for most jobs in the process sector and these are becoming the standards for the industry across the UK. These are known as the "Gold Standards". The Skills Academy is also accrediting those delivering apprenticeships and courses into the sector, effectively, approving quality of delivery and course content. COGENT also operate a very effective career web site known as the "Career Pathway" covering all the sub sectors of the Process Industry. It shows detailed job profiles and key skill requirements for most roles in the sector as well as career options.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Attracting_young_people_into_science_and_engineering">Attracting young people into science and engineering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Attracting young people into science and engineering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Regardless of gender, race or ethnicity, interest in science begins in early childhood.  Nearly 60 percent of scientists say they first became interested in science by age 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Furthermore, surveys have shown that 95% of Primary School Teachers are "uncomfortable" teaching science.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> In the UK at primary school level only 3% of teachers
hold a specialist degree and Initial Teacher Training
(ITT) qualification in science.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Therefore, the Cluster has focused most of its efforts in encouraging children into science and engineering in primary schools and improving teaching resources by supporting the Children Challenging Industry (CCI) Programme, a curriculum-based science learning activity linked to field trips into industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:219px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Children_Challenging_Industry_cartoon_picture.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="187" data-file-width="217" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f1/Children_Challenging_Industry_cartoon_picture.jpg" width="217"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Children_Challenging_Industry_cartoon_picture.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Children Challenging Industry (CCI) attracting Children to Science, Training and Resourcing Primary Teachers</div></div></div>
<p>This programme was initiated in this region by Thomas Swan of Thomas Swan and Co. Ltd. In the early 1990s Tom Swan recognised the need to engage with school children about the role of the chemical industry in our society, and commissioned a three year programme with the Chemical Industry Education Centre (CIEC, now the Centre for Industry Education Collaboration) at the University of York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The Children Challenging Industry Programme was created with the aim, to not only give primary school children an experience of science in action in industry, but also to train primary school teachers how to teach science and where to find science teaching resources. The programme includes specially designed classroom sessions with practical experiments, to capture children's interest, training for the teachers and then industrial site visits<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> to see the science taught put into action. At the start of the lessons the children often perceive industry as "noisy, dark and hot". After the Children Challenging Industry experience 90% of children completing questionnaires demonstrated a more positive and informed attitude towards the industry and the desirability of a career in industry. Studies have shown that 92% of the children enjoyed the industrial experience of science and 98% of teachers reported that the training was either excellent or good.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p>The CCI programme has operated in this region since its inception in the 1990s and its effectiveness has undergone regular evaluation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> To demonstrate the impact, over a 10 year period from 1998-2007, 48,000 children, 9,500 teachers in 1600 schools received the programme across the North of England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> 
Studies in secondary schools of pupils that have received a Children Challenging Industry Experience found that 66% of the pupils remembered learning about industry and were significantly more likely to have positive views about industry and science, in fact 40% of the secondary school pupils responded that the CCI lessons had helped with subsequent science classes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010 Tom Swan received the NEPIC Cluster Life Time Achievement Award from his peers in the process sector for his work in the development and support of Children Challenging Industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> In 2007, and in 2013 he received an honorary degree form the University of York, the NEPIC CCI teacher Ms Nicola Waller won a national award from the Institute of Physics as the UK's best Primary School Science Teacher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Some Cluster members have grown their own staff development programmes using this CCI model, Johnson Matthey for example has created their future scientist programme out of this CCI activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Such activity complements the company's "sustainabilty" and "reputation in the community" programmes. Due in part to the effectiveness of the Children Challenging Industry (CCI)programme some educationalists now contend that laboratory based school science teaching needs to be complemented by out‐of‐school science learning that draws on the actual world (e.g. through field trips to industry etc.), the presented world (e.g. in science centres, botanic gardens, zoos and science museums), and the virtual worlds that are increasingly available through information technologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Turning_interrelated_sectors_into_a_cluster">Turning interrelated sectors into a cluster</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Turning interrelated sectors into a cluster">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NEPIC_Cluster_Symbol.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="436" data-file-width="1544" height="62" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/NEPIC_Cluster_Symbol.jpg/220px-NEPIC_Cluster_Symbol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/NEPIC_Cluster_Symbol.jpg/330px-NEPIC_Cluster_Symbol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/NEPIC_Cluster_Symbol.jpg/440px-NEPIC_Cluster_Symbol.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NEPIC_Cluster_Symbol.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NEPIC logo and sectors</div></div></div>
<p>In 1989, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Porter" title="Michael Porter">Michael Porter</a> said "Clusters are groups of inter-related industries that drive wealth creation in a region". Even in 2017 these concepts are still of academic interest<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> and at the beginning of the 21st century continue to drive industrial policy in growing economies. For example in India<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> and Malaysia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> news articles and research papers still promote Porter's approach to economic development, adding that clusters "typically include the entire value chain of a broadly defined industry from suppliers to end products, and are interconnected by the flow of goods and services throughout this chain. They help improve resource efficiency, time management as well as bring in innovation in manufacturing practices." This notion of broad science-based industries linking together to address cross cutting issues such as growth, sustainability, skills, innovation, infrastructure, stakeholder engagement, sharing best practice and providing a significant representational voice is what brought together the chemical, pharmaceutical, polymer, speciality materials, biotechnology and renewable energy and materials companies based in the northeast of England to create a cluster body to coordinate their work.
</p><p>NEPIC has two offices in the region: one in the north in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunderland,_Tyne_and_Wear" title="Sunderland, Tyne and Wear">Sunderland</a> and one in the south at <a href="/wiki/Wilton,_Redcar_and_Cleveland" title="Wilton, Redcar and Cleveland">Wilton</a> near Redcar in Teesside. At the Wilton location, NEPIC is amongst several process sector and supply chain companies that work out of the process industry research centre <a href="/wiki/Wilton_International" title="Wilton International">Wilton International</a>. The UK Innovation Catapult, the  Centre for Process Innovation, is also based in this multi-occupancy technical development centre.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chemicals">Chemicals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Chemicals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The chemical companies in the membership of NEPIC can be categorised into three groups: <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">petrochemical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commodity_chemicals" title="Commodity chemicals">commodity chemical</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fine_chemicals" title="Fine chemicals">fine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Speciality_chemicals" title="Speciality chemicals">speciality chemical</a> companies. The petrochemical and commodity chemical companies are those most likely to utilise large infrastructure such as pipelines, storage facilities, utilities, power stations, port facilities and railways. These companies in this Cluster are almost exclusively based on Teesside, mostly on three chemical industrial parks at <a href="/wiki/Wilton,_Redcar_and_Cleveland" title="Wilton, Redcar and Cleveland">Wilton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billingham" title="Billingham">Billingham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seal_Sands" title="Seal Sands">Seal Sands</a>. Examples of large scale commodity manufacturers in the NEPIC Cluster are Sabic making ethylene, low-density polyethylene and aromatics, <a href="/wiki/Ineos" title="Ineos">Ineos</a> acrylonitrile, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GrowHow" title="GrowHow">GrowHow</a> ammonia and ammonia based fertilzers, Ensus bioethanol and animal feed, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conoco_Phillips" title="Conoco Phillips">Conoco Phillips</a> oil refining, <a href="/wiki/Omya" title="Omya">Omya</a> Calcium Carbonate, <a href="/wiki/Huntsman_Corporation" title="Huntsman Corporation">Huntsman</a> polyurathane intermediates and titanium dioxide, Harvest Energy biodiesel and <a href="/wiki/Greenergy" title="Greenergy">Greenergy</a> fuel blending. These commodity chemical companies used to share logistical, utility and other infrastructure with Sahaviriya Steel Industries (SSI) who made steel in <a href="/wiki/Redcar_and_Cleveland" title="Redcar and Cleveland">Redcar</a> until final closure in October 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> This was Europe's second largest operational blast furnace. <a href="/wiki/Tata_Steel" title="Tata Steel">TATA</a> Steel still operate steel milling and rolling units on Teesside.
</p><p>The speciality chemical and fine chemical companies in the NEPIC Cluster are spread across all the sub-regions of northeast England including Teesside, <a href="/wiki/County_Durham" title="County Durham">County Durham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear" title="Tyne and Wear">Tyne and Wear</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northumberland" title="Northumberland">Northumberland</a>. Examples on Teesside: Fine Organics, Chemoxy, Vertellus, <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Matthey" title="Johnson Matthey">Johnson Matthey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koppers" title="Koppers">Koppers</a>, Lucite International and <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Chemical_Corporation" title="Mitsubishi Chemical Corporation">Mitsubishi Chemicals</a>. In County Durham: High Force Research, Newchem Technologies, Thomas Swan, Exwold Technology and Huntsman Tioxide, and Frutarom. In Tyne and Wear and Northumberland Kilfrost, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akzo" title="Akzo">Akzo</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/International_Paint" title="International Paint">International Paint</a> and Chemson all manufacture speciality chemicals while Aesica, Sterling Pharma Solutions and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piramal_Enterprises_Ltd" title="Piramal Enterprises Ltd">Piramal</a> make and use fine chemical intermediates mostly as pharmaceutical intermediates. Companies in the NEPIC footprint are also involved in the scale up, manufacture and commercialisation of <a href="/wiki/Graphene" title="Graphene">Graphene</a>, Applied Graphene Materials<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> and Thomas Swan Limited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The UK Government has also chosen this Cluster to base its National Graphene Applications Centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>The above chemical companies are also supported by specialist utility providers and speciality gas providers such as Sembcorp and BOC-Linde, bulk storage businesses such as Simon Storage and <a href="/wiki/Vopak" title="Vopak">Vopak</a>, while speciality packaging and formulation of chemicals is provided by companies such as Banner Chemicals, MP Storage and Exwold who also all operate Teesside facilities. Throughout the whole region <a href="/wiki/Northumbrian_Water" title="Northumbrian Water">Northumbrian Water</a> can provide bulk water and also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waste_water_treatment" title="Waste water treatment">waste water treatment</a> facilities to the all sectors of the process industry. The region is self-sufficient in water and can allocate industrial quantities to new investors due to the development of the <a href="/wiki/Kielder_Water" title="Kielder Water">Kielder Reservoir</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polymers">Polymers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Polymers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Polymer manufacturing in the northeast of England Process Industry Cluster has some large-scale activity based on Teesside. SABIC operate one of the world's biggest <a href="/wiki/Low-density_polyethylene" title="Low-density polyethylene">low-density polyethylene</a> (LDPE) plants,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> which makes the United Kingdom a net exporter of LDPE. Lotte Chemical manufacture both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Purified_terephthalic_acid" title="Purified terephthalic acid">purified terephthalic acid</a> (PTA) and <a href="/wiki/Polyethylene_terephthalate" title="Polyethylene terephthalate">polyethylene terephthalate</a> (PET). <a href="/wiki/Ineos" title="Ineos">Ineos</a> manufacture <a href="/wiki/Acrylonitrile" title="Acrylonitrile">acrylonitrile</a>, an intermediate used for <a href="/wiki/Nylon_66" title="Nylon 66">Nylon 66</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acrylate_polymer" title="Acrylate polymer">acrylics</a>. Speciality polymer products are also made there. Ineos, for example, also manufacture aqueous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polyvinylchloride" title="Polyvinylchloride">polyvinylchloride</a> PVC products in County Durham whilst <a href="/wiki/Victrex" title="Victrex">Victrex</a> manufacture all the monomer for their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PEEK" title="PEEK">polyether ether ketone (PEEK)</a> product at their facility on Teesside. There are also new biopolymers and resins in development and scale up by companies such as Plaxica, which is developing new processes to commercialise <a href="/wiki/Polylactic_acid" title="Polylactic acid">polylactic acid</a> (PLA) and Cambridge Biopolymers, who are commercialising functional bioresins; both are based at the Teesside process industry research centre <a href="/wiki/Wilton_International" title="Wilton International">Wilton International</a>.
</p><p>New processes for the recycling of polymers have also been commercialised at Wilton. For example, Biffa Polymers recycle a large percentage of the UK's plastic milk bottles into polymer chip. This was one of the first technology applications which allowed food-grade polymer packaging to be recycled without passing through a melted phase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> In 2013, <a href="/wiki/SNF_Floerger" title="SNF Floerger">SNF</a> announced that they intend to build a polymer manufacturing unit on Teesside to make <a href="/wiki/Polyacrylamide" title="Polyacrylamide">polyacrylamide</a> emulsion for the oil industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Although not strictly a polymer, the acrylic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perspex" title="Perspex">Perspex</a> is a well known plastic like material; it and other acrylic products are manufactured in Teesside and County Durham by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lucite" title="Lucite">Lucite International</a>, which is a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi" title="Mitsubishi">Mitsubishi corporation</a>.
</p><p>The region also has a significant number of polymer extrusion and forming companies that supply a number of advanced engineering supply chains<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> notably the automobile supply chain which, in northeast England, is dominated by <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a>'s European automobile manufacturing plant at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunderland,_Tyne_and_Wear" title="Sunderland, Tyne and Wear">Sunderland</a>. The automobile supply chain in this region is represented by the North East Automobile Alliance (NEAA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pharmaceuticals">Pharmaceuticals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Pharmaceuticals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This region has an active, modern pharmaceutical industry and the northeast of England has a full capability in the pharmaceutical <a href="/wiki/Value_chain" title="Value chain">value chain</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Drug_discovery" title="Drug discovery">pre-clinical drug discovery</a> and development, clinical research and development, <a href="/wiki/Clinical_trial" title="Clinical trial">clinical trial</a> management, pilot-scale manufacturing, full-scale pharmaceutical ingredient and intermediate manufacturing, as well as final product formulation, packaging and distribution. Furthermore, pharmaceutical businesses are underpinned by an experienced and successful supply chain. Within the NEPIC cluster there are companies that provide laboratory facilities, manufacturing sites, logistics, construction and procurement, analytical sciences, validation consultants, maintenance, operation and financial services, public relations and contingency planning.
</p><p>Fundamental <a href="/wiki/Medical_research" title="Medical research">medical research</a> is done in this region at several of its universities. For example, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University" title="Newcastle University">Newcastle University</a> was the first to receive a licence in the UK to perform research on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stem_cells" title="Stem cells">stem cells</a> and this is a leading centre for such research today. Indeed <a href="/wiki/Karim_Nayernia" title="Karim Nayernia">Karim Nayernia</a> was the first to isolate spermatagonial stem cells at this University. Many new healthcare developments have arisen from this research work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup>
</p><p>Industrial <a href="/wiki/Drug_development" title="Drug development">drug development</a> continues at ARCINOVA in Alnwick. Small molecule drug <a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">scale-up</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Process_development" title="Process development">process development</a> and manufacture is provided to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Current_good_manufacturing_practice" title="Current good manufacturing practice">current good manufacturing practice</a>(cGMP) standards to pharmaceutical companies around the world by several NEPIC Cluster members such as Aesica Pharmaceuticals, Sterling Pharma Solutions, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piramal_Enterprises_Ltd" title="Piramal Enterprises Ltd">Piramal</a> Healthcare, all of which are based in <a href="/wiki/Northumberland" title="Northumberland">Northumberland</a> and also by Fine Organics on <a href="/wiki/Teesside" title="Teesside">Teesside</a>. Aesica, Sterling, Piramal (Northumberland) are companies that perform primary manufacture of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Active_pharmaceutical_ingredients" title="Active pharmaceutical ingredients">active pharmaceutical ingredients</a>(APIs) to cGMP standards. While Aesica, Piramal, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merck_Sharp_and_Dohme" title="Merck Sharp and Dohme">MSD</a> (Northumberland), <a href="/wiki/Sanofi" title="Sanofi">Sanofi</a> (Tyne &amp; Wear), <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a>, Quantum Pharmaceuticals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> and Bristol Laboratories<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> in (County Durham) are all secondary pharmaceutical manufacturers with large facilities in the region. These companies formulate and package finished pharmaceuticals ready for consumer use. Small quantity and speciality pharmaceutical formulations are also manufactured by contract manufacturers Specials Labs and SCM Pharma in Northumberland, which was acquired by Shire Pharmaceuticals in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> While Fujifilm Diosynth Biotechnologies (Teesside), formerly Avecia is one of the largest investments in the world in <a href="/wiki/Biopharmaceutical" title="Biopharmaceutical">biopharmaceutical</a> &amp; biologics medicines manufacturing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> the company manufactures, under contract, active biopharmaceuticals for a number of pharmaceutical companies. Pharmaceuticals make up a significant proportion of the exports of the northeast of England. The region produces 33% of the UK's GDP in pharmaceutical 
manufacturing with 95% of finished product exported to global markets<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biotechnology">Biotechnology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Biotechnology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Biotechnology has become widely used in many industrial and academic activities and the following classifications have become established. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Biotechnology" title="Red Biotechnology">Red Biotechnology</a> – Medical, Health care and Pharmaceutical Biotechnology. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Biotechnology" title="White Biotechnology">White Biotechnology</a> - Biotechnology for industrial products. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_Biotechnology" title="Green Biotechnology">Green Biotechnology</a> - Biotechnology applied to environmental issues. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_Biotechnology" title="Blue Biotechnology">Blue Biotechnology</a> - Biotechnology based on marine organisms. The northeast of England has strengths in all these areas.
</p><p>Industrial and academic biotechnological research in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Biotechnology" title="Red Biotechnology">Red Biotechnology</a> has been well established in the northeast England and has developed into strengths in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diagnostics" title="Diagnostics">diagnostics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bioinformatics" title="Bioinformatics">bioinformatics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biomanufacturing" title="Biomanufacturing">Biomanufacturing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biocatalysis_%26_Biotransformation" title="Biocatalysis &amp; Biotransformation">Biocatalysis &amp; Bio-transformations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bioremediation" title="Bioremediation">Bioremediation</a>, Pharmaceutical research, Microbiological analysis and testing, Production of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antibodies" title="Antibodies">antibodies</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proteins" title="Proteins">proteins</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peptides" title="Peptides">peptides</a>. Leading edge research is done at the region's Universities, for example <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University" title="Newcastle University">Newcastle University</a> was the first institution in Europe, second in the world, to receive permission to pursue stem-cell research in human embryos.
</p><p>New industries that have now developed form a significant sector in the Northeast of England Process Industry Cluster (NEPIC). Fujifilm Diosynth Biologics at Billingham now employs over 550 people, the majority of them being graduate-level skills in biotechnology, to develop new products and innovative processes for the pharmaceutical industry. Within a mile of the Fujifilm complex are small companies working on the building blocks of life. Cambridge Research Biochemicals (CRB) supports discovery research activities by providing custom-made research reagents, principally peptides and antibodies. In Sunderland, Immuno Diagnostic Systems (IDS) are producing medical test kits and in Hartlepool Hart Biologicals produce diagnostic products for use in the detection, prevention, and monitoring of a number of medical conditions. In Morpeth, Northumberland <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piramal_Healthcare" title="Piramal Healthcare">Piramal Healthcare</a> invested into bio-pharmaceutical manufacturing facilities.
</p><p>Across the region, companies such as Leica Biosystems, Orla Proteins, Helena Bioscience, Thermo Fischer Scientific and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millipore_Corporation" title="Millipore Corporation">Millipore</a> are significant contributors to the growing strength of the sector and its supply chain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>Industrial, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Biotechnology" title="White Biotechnology">White Biotechnology</a> includes manufacturing, alternative energy (or "bioenergy"), and biomaterials and is also well established in the region. The manufacturers of the food protein Quorn, Marlow Foods, now part of <a href="/wiki/Premier_Foods" title="Premier Foods">Premier Foods</a>, developed their technology here and still operate in this region. <a href="/wiki/Northumbrian_Water" title="Northumbrian Water">Northumbrian Water</a> has invested in two large scale <a href="/wiki/Anaerobic_digestion" title="Anaerobic digestion">anaerobic digestion</a> facilities to recover energy from their domestic and industrial waste water streams. In <a href="/wiki/Stockton-on-Tees" title="Stockton-on-Tees">Stockton-on-Tees</a>, Cleveland Biotechnology has been pioneering natural solutions to handling effluents and waste materials. In <a href="/wiki/Billingham" title="Billingham">Billingham</a>, Biochemica is applying new biotechnology solutions to industrial water treatment. Biotechnology is also being applied to manufacture polymers by Plaxica and functional resins by Cambridge Biopolymers. Several of the Cluster's Fine and Specialty chemical companies are utilising enzymatic transformations in their manufacturing processes. Developments such as these are being supported by The Centre for Process Innovation (CPI) which hosts the National Industrial Biotechnology Facility (NIBF) at <a href="/wiki/Wilton_International" title="Wilton International">Wilton International</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewables_and_bioresources">Renewables and bioresources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Renewables and bioresources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Members of the North East England Process Industry Cluster (NEPIC) are also focusing on development of <a href="/wiki/Biorefinery" title="Biorefinery">biorefinery</a> concepts which could impact on fine, speciality and <a href="/wiki/Commodity_chemicals" title="Commodity chemicals">commodity chemicals</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals" title="Pharmaceuticals">pharmaceuticals</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agrochemicals" title="Agrochemicals">agrochemicals</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bio-fuels" title="Bio-fuels">bio-fuels</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bioethanol" title="Bioethanol">bioethanol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Large scale biofuels plants are already operating on <a href="/wiki/Teesside" title="Teesside">Teesside</a> by Ensus and Harvest Energy, while <a href="/wiki/Greenergy" title="Greenergy">Greenergy</a> (note: Harvest and Greenergy are all now part of the Interterminals Group) operate a biofuel blending facility. <a href="/wiki/CF_Industries" title="CF Industries">CF Industries</a> (formerly GrowHow) who manufacture fertilizer is capturing <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> from their ammonia based fertilizer business and this is being used to aid the growing of tomatoes in an industrial market garden on Teesside.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> This reduces emissions and eliminates road miles from former European imports. Sembcorp operate a 30 MW biomass power plant known as Wilton 10 using both waste wood and coppiced wood, which is integrated into the existing chemical processes on the Wilton Chemical Site. A number of other biomass and waste to energy plants are in development within the Cluster such as Wilton 11<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> and MGT Power are building their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teesport_Renewable_Energy_Plant" title="Teesport Renewable Energy Plant">Teesport Renewable Energy Plant</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> SITA already operate an energy from waste unit in Middlesbrough. Many of the Cluster companies working on Renewables and Bioresources projects to develop a lower carbon future for the sector collaborate through the NEPIC Clusters Bioresources Collaborative Thrust Team. The Cluster's growing strength in low carbon, sustainable industry has gained national recognition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>The drive to industrialise <a href="/wiki/Biorefinery" title="Biorefinery">biorefinery</a> technologies within the NEPIC Cluster is mostly aimed at reducing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_emissions" title="Carbon emissions">carbon emissions</a> or at making manufacturing more sustainable by counterbalancing the emissions by the reabsorption of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> through the growth of an equivalent amount of biomass. Alternatively they are implementing technologies that enable the use of societal waste as a new basic raw material. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemical_Engineering" title="Chemical Engineering">Chemical Engineering</a> technologies that are being implemented include advanced <a href="/wiki/Gasification" title="Gasification">gasification</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_Products" title="Air Products">Air Products</a> are implementing their <a href="/wiki/Plasma_gasification" title="Plasma gasification">plasma gasification</a> technology on Teesside, the company has announced that a second such unit is also to be built in this location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Others are developing projects utilising <a href="/wiki/Pyrolysis" title="Pyrolysis">pyrolysis</a> to recover useful materials from carbon wastes and also new processes to manufacture <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synthetic_natural_gas" title="Synthetic natural gas">biosynthetic natural gas</a> (SNG)and fuels from air being developed by Air Fuels Synthesis. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Depolymerisation" title="Depolymerisation">Depolymerisation</a> processes are also under investigation.
</p><p>The Cluster companies and new investors collaborating through the Northeast of England Process Industry Cluster (NEPIC) on renewables and bioresources projects do so through the Cluster's Bioresources Thrust Team.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporting_and_developing_an_extensive_supply_chain">Supporting and developing an extensive supply chain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Supporting and developing an extensive supply chain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Chemical, Pharmaceutical, Speciality, Biotechnology companies cannot operate without the support of an extensive local <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain" title="Supply chain">supply chain</a>. Supply Chain companies within NEPIC include <a href="/wiki/Analytical_chemistry" title="Analytical chemistry">Analytical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Measurement_Science_and_Technology" title="Measurement Science and Technology">Measurement Science</a> Companies, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemical_Engineering" title="Chemical Engineering">Chemical Engineering</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Control_Engineering" title="Control Engineering">Control Engineering</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mechanical_Engineering" title="Mechanical Engineering">Mechanical Engineering</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Process_Engineering" title="Process Engineering">Process Engineering</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_engineering_methodology" title="Project engineering methodology">Project Engineering</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Construction_Engineering" title="Construction Engineering">Construction Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maintenance_engineering" title="Maintenance engineering">Maintenance Engineering</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toolmaker" title="Toolmaker">Toolmakers</a>, Business and Site Security, <a href="/wiki/Safety_management_systems" title="Safety management systems">Safety Management</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disaster_management" title="Disaster management">Disaster</a> and Business Recovery Management, Engineering Equipment Suppliers, Laboratory Equipment Suppliers, Business Performance Improvement Consultants, Legal Firms, Management &amp; Strategy Consultants, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Process_development" title="Process development">Process Development</a>, Publicity Firms, Publishers and Printers, Purchasing Companies, Recruitment Companies, Research Institutions etc.
</p><p>The Cluster Leadership Team believe that the promotion of the capability of these supply chain companies is crucial to its ability to attract investment to the region.  Furthermore the Cluster promotes its supply chain members' businesses around the world to help them secure more business, locally, nationally and internationally.
</p><p>The concentration of such supply chain businesses in the northeast of England is internationally significant. In 2009 Service Network commissioned Shared Intelligence and Gavurin to undertake an assessment of the Knowledge Intensive Business &amp; Services (KIBS) sector in the northeast of England. The report concludes that KIBS companies are distributed across the whole of the region. It identifies that the region has a particular strength in Architectural &amp; Engineering Activities &amp; Related Technical Consultancy (AETC) workplaces with 2810 such firms employing 13,385 people. The report also identifies that the concentration of ATEC business is the highest in the UK and around <a href="/wiki/Stockton-on-Tees" title="Stockton-on-Tees">Stockton-on-Tees</a> the concentration is amongst the highest for such businesses in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_of_clusters_such_as_NEPIC_in_globalised_industries">Role of clusters such as NEPIC in globalised industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Role of clusters such as NEPIC in globalised industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to Christian Ketels of <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Business_School" title="Harvard Business School">Harvard Business School</a> "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Globalisation" title="Globalisation">Globalisation</a> has not only raised the relative role of location and Clusters, it has raised the bar in terms of the demands that successful clusters have to meet."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Ketels suggests that this is because competition between clusters has increased and rival locations are vying for any new investment in their sectors. It is this that pressurises Cluster organisations to meet the best practice of clusters in other regions. Such competition has driven clusters to become more specialised and there is now much more differentiation, for example, some clusters are R&amp;D Hubs while others focus on manufacturing or are service orientated. Ketels' premise is that this increasing level of specialisation has increased linkages between cluster bodies and that the ability of the cluster management teams to make such linkages and partnerships has become an important key strength. In the past, Ketels suggests, clusters were like islands competing with each other whereas now they are part of Global supply chains often competing and co-operating at the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ketels' observations are borne out by the work of the Northeast of England Process Industry Cluster (NEPIC) which uses its cluster to cluster links in two ways to meet the strategic needs of its Industrial Leadership Council. Firstly, to meet its Internationalisation aims, NEPIC's cluster to cluster activities build up a wider international understanding of the capabilities of the industry in its region and also of its members specific businesses. Secondly, it uses cluster to cluster relationships to help develop the business, particularly of its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Small_and_Medium_Enterprise" title="Small and Medium Enterprise">Small and Medium Enterprise</a> (SME) members, with the aim of strengthening SME businesses in its local supply chain. NEPIC does this by using its international linkages and partnerships to de-risk the initial development of international trade for its members. This is achieved by reciprocal knowledge and support of partner clusters and trade bodies and their members. NEPIC's approach is to develop formal Memoranda of Understanding (MOUs)with industry clusters and business associations around the world and build partnerships to create knowledge sharing opportunities.
</p><p>In Europe, NEPIC has projects and agreements with the following Cluster bodies: Axelera,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> and through the WIINTECH consortium, Plastipolis in France, Proplast in Italy, Chemie-Cluster Bayern (CCB) in Germany, Clusterland in Austria, Plastival in Spain, Veneto Nanotech in Italy and Poolnet in Portugal. In India, with the Indian Chemical Council (ICC),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> the Karnataka Drug and Pharmaceutical Manufacturers Association (KDPMA),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Gujarat Chemical Association, Vapi Industries Association,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Mangalore Special Economic Zone (MSEZ) and <a href="/wiki/Plastindia" title="Plastindia">Plastindia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> In Brazil, with the Suape Coplexo Industria Portuario<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> and in China the Jiangsu Association of Science and Technology (JASTI). NEPIC has participated in joint meetings and projects with these organisations and has often managed reciprocal visits from groups of companies associated with the aforementioned bodies and countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>These partnerships can lead to joint projects, for example, NEPIC and the Indian Chemical Council (ICC) jointly organised the Indian Chemical Industry Outlook Conference in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Furthermore member companies have found new business via such Cluster to Cluster relationships, for example one SME business attending the Indian Outlook Conference in India in 2013 reported in the market visit blog that "the quality, seniority and number of attendees that NEPIC (and ICC) have attracted are of great credit to them. I have calculated that it would have taken me at least 4 years to meet the executives that have met in one week on this trip."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> At the same time others reported new business being created during their first market visit with the Cluster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>
</p><p>By 2017 NEPIC had become a key partner of the Indian Chemical Council (ICC) helping to define the agenda for their Annual Outlook Conference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> The 2017 NEPIC led and UK <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Trade" title="Department for International Trade">Department for International Trade</a> (DIT) <a href="/wiki/Trade_mission" title="Trade mission">trade mission</a> to India had grown to include 21 business delegates who travelled to <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pune" title="Pune">Pune</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> meeting companies  the company members of the <a href="/wiki/Karnataka" title="Karnataka">Karnataka</a> Drug and Pharmaceutical Association (KDPMA), <a href="/wiki/Tata_Research_Development_and_Design_Centre" title="Tata Research Development and Design Centre">Tata Research Development and Design Centre</a> and the members of the Indian Chemical Council. With companies such as Jacobs Engineering, SMEs such as Biochimica UK Limited (water treatment), Micropore Technologies Limited (innovative dispersion &amp; emulsification technology)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> and Harrison Goddard Foote (HGF)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> (patent agents) being very positive about their experience and showing the supply chain diversity. These companies show the diversity of the chemical process industry <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain" title="Supply chain">supply chain</a>.
</p>
